## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics (ODE growth models)
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is an explicit time-derivative of population size P, indicating a continuous-time population growth ODE. With only (t, P) available, the most common structures are density-independent growth, density-dependent regulation (carrying capacity), Allee effects, harvesting/immigration terms, and time-varying (e.g., seasonal) growth rates.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential (Malthusian) growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent per-capita growth)
- Linear time-trend in per-capita growth: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P (changing environment over time)
- Quadratic density dependence (logistic ODE): dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 (crowding reduces growth)
- Carrying-capacity form: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (equivalent logistic with K = 1/c1)
- Theta-logistic ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (nonlinear density dependence strength)
- Gompertz ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (multiplicative growth with log-density feedback)
- Richards (generalized logistic) ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2)**c3 (flexible sigmoidal regulation)
- Allee effect (strong) ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P) (negative growth below a threshold)
- Allee effect (weak) rational form: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P + c1) / (P + c2) - c3 * P**2 (facilitation at low P, competition at high P)
- Constant immigration with density dependence: dP_dt = c0 + c1 * P - c2 * P**2 (influx plus crowding)
- Proportional harvesting (effort ∝ P): dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 - c2 * P (removal linear in population)
- Constant-yield harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 - c2 (fixed off-take/harvest)
- Seasonal forcing in growth rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P - c4 * P**2 (periodic environment)
- Time-varying carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - P / (c1 + c2 * t + c3 * sin(c4 * t + c5))) (resource base changes over time)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Density-independent growth → dP_dt proportional to P; per-capita rate (dP_dt/P) approximately constant
- Crowding/competition → negative curvature at high P, commonly modeled by a -P**2 term or (1 - c*P) factor
- Nonlinear density regulation strength → (c*P)**theta inside the limiting term to shift how sharply regulation turns on
- Allee effects (mate limitation/cooperation) → factors like (P - A) or increasing per-capita growth at low P, producing possible extinction threshold
- Gompertz-type regulation → dP_dt proportional to P*log(K/P), giving slower approach to carrying capacity and asymmetric trajectories
- External inputs/removals → additive constants (immigration) or subtractive terms (harvest), changing equilibria and allowing negative growth even at moderate P
- Seasonality or cyclic resources → sinusoidal forcing in coefficients multiplying P (time-varying per-capita growth)
- Regime shifts over time → coefficients that drift with t (e.g., c0 + c1*t) capturing long-term environmental change
- Multiple equilibria → cubic-like dependence in P (e.g., P*(P-A)*(1-cP)) indicating bistability and tipping points

Let \(k=0.9909642091509507\).  
GT:
\[
k(1-\tfrac{P}{39.01184604772507})P + kP^{1/3}+kP
= kP^{1/3} + (2k)P - \Big(\tfrac{k}{39.01184604772507}\Big)P^2
\]
So GT is **independent of \(t\)** and is exactly a linear combination of \(P^{1/3}, P, P^2\) with **no constant term** and no other \(P\)-powers.

Therefore, any candidate can match iff it can be reduced (by choosing its constants) to
\[
A\,P^{1/3} + B\,P + C\,P^2
\]
with \(A=k,\; B=2k,\; C=-k/39.01184604772507\), and with all \(t\)-dependent parts eliminated.

### 1–27 (all contain unavoidable non-polynomial-in-\(P\) or \(t\)-dependent structure unless zeroed)
1. \(+\;c3\sin(c4 t+c5)\): set \(c3=0\) → reduces to \(c0P^{1/3}+c1P^2+c2P\) (possible).  
2. sine term: set sine amplitude \(c4=0\) (or \(c3=0\)) → reduces to \(c0P^{1/3}+c1P^2+(c2+c3)P\) (possible).  
3. \(c3 e^{c4 t}\): set \(c3=0\) → reduces to base polynomial (possible).  
4. \(c4 e^{c5 t}\): set \(c4=0\) → reduces to base polynomial (possible).  
5. \(P\cdot c3(c4+t)^{c5}\): set \(c3=0\) → base polynomial (possible).  
6. \(P\cdot c4(c5+t)^{c6}\): set \(c4=0\) → base polynomial (possible).  
7. rational-in-\(t\) terms: set \(c4=0\) and \(c7=0\) (or make both numerators 0) → base polynomial (possible).  
8. rational-in-\(t\): set \(c3=0,c6=0\) → base polynomial (possible).  
9. \(\frac{P c3}{c4 t+c5}+\frac{c6}{c4 t+c5}\): set \(c3=0,c6=0\) → base polynomial (possible).  
10. similar: set \(c4=0,c7=0\) → base polynomial (possible).  
11. \(c3 t^{c4}\): set \(c3=0\) → base polynomial (possible).  
12. \(c4 t^{c5}\): set \(c4=0\) → base polynomial (possible).  
13. \(c4\log(c5 t+1)\): set \(c4=0\) → base polynomial (possible).  
14. \(c3\log(c4 t+1)\): set \(c3=0\) → base polynomial (possible).  
15. has \(tanh(\cdot)\): set \(c4=0\); remaining \(P^2,P,P^{c2}\). Can match only if choose \(c2=1/3\) and coefficients accordingly (possible).  
16. has \(\sin(Pc5+c6)\): must set \(c4=0\); then same as (15) without tanh (possible with \(c2=1/3\)).  
17. has \(\sin(Pc6+c7)\): set \(c5=0\); then \(P^2,P,P,P^{c3}\) (possible with \(c3=1/3\)).  
18. \(c4 t (P+c5)^{c6}\): set \(c4=0\) → base polynomial (possible).  
19. \(P^2 c1\tanh(\cdot)\): to remove \(t\)-dependence must set \(c1=0\); then only \(P^{1/3}\) and \(P\) remain, cannot create required \(P^2\) term ⇒ **cannot** match.  
20. \(c3 t (P+c4)^{c5}\): set \(c3=0\) → base polynomial (possible).  
21. \(c3 t + c4\): to remove \(t\) set \(c3=0\), but then constant \(c4\) must be 0 too; reduces to base polynomial (possible).  
22. \(c4 t + c5\): set \(c4=0,c5=0\) → base polynomial (possible).  
23–24. rational terms in \(P\): to avoid non-polynomial dependence, set their numerators to 0 (e.g., \(c4=0,c7=0\) etc.) → base polynomial (possible).  
25–26. \(\exp(Pc4)\): must set exponential amplitude to 0 (set \(c3=0\) or \(c4=0\) depending) → base polynomial (possible).  
27. contains \(P\cdot t\) and \(t\) terms: must set coefficients of all \(t\)-dependent terms to 0 (e.g., \(c3=c4=c7=0\)); then left with \(P^2,P,P,P^{c5}\) (possible with \(c5=1/3\)).  

So far: only #19 is structurally impossible; many others can be reduced to the needed 3-term form.

### 28–36 (pure polynomial-in-\(P\) forms or with extra constants)
28. \(c0P^{1/3}+c1P^2+c2P\): exactly the needed basis ⇒ **can match** by setting  
\(c0=k,\; c1=-k/39.01184604772507,\; c2=2k\).
29. same but extra \(P c3\): combine into \(P\) coefficient ⇒ can match (choose \(c2+c3=2k\)).  
30. has fixed \(P^{1/3}\) coefficient 1 plus \(P^{c2}\): can still match by setting \(c3=0\) and forcing \(1\) to equal \(k\), impossible since 1≠k ⇒ **cannot** match.  
31. includes \(+P\) with fixed coefficient 1: would require \(1=2k\), false ⇒ **cannot** match.  
32. includes extra fixed \(P^{1/3}\): coefficient becomes \(c0+1\), can set \(c0=k-1\) ⇒ can match.  
33. \(P^2,P,P,P^{c3}\): can match by setting \(c3=1/3\) and coefficients accordingly.  
34. has extra \(P c4\) and constant \(c5\): set \(c5=0\), combine \(P\) coefficients ⇒ can match.  
35. has constant \(c3\): must set \(c3=0\) ⇒ then can match.  
36. has constant \(c4\): set \(c4=0\) ⇒ then can match.

### 37–47 (extra exp/log/tanh terms)
37. \(+\;c4 e^{Pc5}\): must set \(c4=0\); then \(P^2,P,P^{c2}\) ⇒ match with \(c2=1/3\).  
38. \(+\;c5 e^{Pc6}\): set \(c5=0\); then \(P^2,P,P,P^{c3}\) ⇒ match with \(c3=1/3\).  
39. \(+\;c5\log(Pc6+1)\): must set \(c5=0\); then match with \(c3=1/3\).  
40. \(+\;c4\log(Pc5+1)\): set \(c4=0\); then match with \(c2=1/3\).  
41. contains \(P*c2*(P*c3)^{c4}\) which is \( \propto P^{c4+1}\) (times constants) plus \(P^{c5}\) and also \(P\) terms; to get \(P^{1/3}\) you’d need \(c5=1/3\). To get \(P^2\) you’d need \(c4+1=2\Rightarrow c4=1\). Then you can tune coefficients; also must ensure no extra independent \(P\) term beyond what you can combine (there are two \(P\) terms \(Pc0+Pc1\), fine). ⇒ can match.  
42. already \(c0P^{1/3}+c1P^2+c2P+c4P^{c3}\): set \(c4=0\) ⇒ match.  
43. has extra \(P^{c4}\): set \(c5=0\) (or \(c4\) such that it duplicates an existing power, but easiest is zero it) ⇒ match.  
44. has \(\log(Pc4+1)\): must set \(c3=0\) ⇒ match.  
45. same with extra \(P c3\): set \(c4=0\) ⇒ match.  
46. has \(\tanh(c1 t+c2)\) multiplying \(P^2\) and also additive tanh term: to remove \(t\), must set both tanh amplitudes \(c0=0\) and \(c6=0\). Then no \(P^2\) term remains ⇒ **cannot** match.  
47. has \(c4\tanh(c5 t)\): set \(c4=0\); then \(P^2,P,P^{c2}\) ⇒ match with \(c2=1/3\).

### 48–55 (rational forms etc.)
48. everything over \((Pc1+c2)\): to become a polynomial for all \(P\), would need \(c1=0\) so denominator constant; then expression becomes a polynomial with powers \(P^{1/3},P^{4/3},P, P^2, P^3\). Must zero out unwanted powers (\(P^{4/3},P^3\)) by setting corresponding numerators \(c0=c4=0\), and combine \(P\) and \(P^2\) terms. Then can match.  
49. has constant \(c4\) and log term: set \(c4=0,c5=0\); then \(P^2,P,P^{c2}\) ⇒ match with \(c2=1/3\).
